这就解释了为什么对犯罪分子的社会学和心理学研究通常含糊不清且收效甚微：它们面对的是两种不同类型的人，而普通的理论或实证框架无法充分区分这两种人。研究赌徒也存在同样的问题。交易分析和博弈分析为此提供了一个直接的解决方案。它们通过在社会层面之下，从交易的角度区分“玩家”和“职业赌徒”，从而消除了这种模糊性。

Let us now turn from this general thesis to consider specific examples. Some burglars do their jobs without any waste motion. The ‘Cops and Robbers’ burglar leaves his calling card in gratuitous acts of vandalism, such as spoiling valuable clothing with secretions and excretions. The straight bank robber, according to reports, takes every possible precaution to avoid violence; the C & R bank robber is only looking for an excuse to vent his anger. Like any professional, a straight criminal likes his jobs to be as clean as circumstances permit. The C & R criminal is compelled to blow off steam in the course of his work. The true professional is said never to operate until the fix is in; the player is willing to take on the law barehanded. Straight professionals are well aware, in their own way, of the game of C & R. If a gang member shows too much interest in the game, to the point of jeopardizing the job, and particularly if his need to be caught begins to show, they will take drastic measures to prevent a recurrence. Perhaps it is just because straight professionals are not playing C & R that they are so seldom caught, and hence so rarely studied sociologically, psychologically and psychiatrically; and this also applies to gamblers. Hence most of our clinical knowledge about criminals and gamblers refers to players rather than to straight professionals.

现在让我们从这个总体论点转向具体的例子。有些窃贼行事干脆利落，毫无浪费。“警察与强盗”式的窃贼则会留下一些无谓的破坏行为作为“标记”，比如用分泌物和排泄物弄脏贵重衣物。据报道，正规的银行劫匪会采取一切可能的预防措施来避免暴力；而“警察与强盗”式的银行劫匪只是想找个借口发泄怒火。像任何专业人士一样，正规的罪犯也希望自己的“工作”尽可能干净利落。“警察与强盗”式的罪犯则需要在作案过程中发泄情绪。据说，真正的专业人士从不在“警察与强盗”式的作案前出手；他们甚至愿意赤手空拳地与法律对抗。正规的专业人士也深谙“警察与强盗”式的规则。如果团伙成员对这种“游戏”表现出过分的兴趣，甚至危及作案，尤其是当他们开始表现出渴望被抓的倾向时，他们会采取极端措施来防止再次作案。或许正是因为职业赌徒不参与非法赌博，所以他们才很少被抓获，因此也很少被从社会学、心理学和精神病学的角度进行研究；这种情况也适用于其他赌徒。因此，我们关于罪犯和赌徒的大部分临床知识都指向的是普通赌徒，而不是职业赌徒。

Kleptomaniacs (as opposed to professional shoplifters) are examples of how widely trivial C & R is played. It is probable that a very large percentage of Occidentals, at least, have played C & R in fantasy, and that is what sells newspapers in our half of the world. This fantasy frequently occurs in the form of dreaming up the ‘perfect murder’, which is playing the hardest possible game and completely outwitting the cops.

有盗窃癖的人（而非职业扒手）就是一个例子，说明这种低俗的犯罪游戏有多么普遍。至少在西方，很可能很大一部分人都曾在幻想中玩过犯罪游戏，而这正是我们这半边世界报纸的畅销之处。这种幻想常常以构思“完美谋杀”的形式出现，也就是玩难度最高的游戏，彻底智胜警察。

Variations of C & R are ‘Auditors and Robbers’, played by embezzlers with the same rules and the same payoff; ‘Customs and Robbers’, played by smugglers, etc. Of special interest is the criminal variation of ‘Courtroom’. Despite all his precautions, the professional may occasionally be arrested and brought to trial. For him’ Courtroom’ is a procedure, which he carries out according to the instructions of his legal advisers. For the lawyers, if they are compulsive winners, ‘Courtroom’ is essentially a game played with the jury in which the object is to win, not lose, and this is regarded as a constructive game by a large segment of society.

“法庭与强盗”游戏的变体包括“审计员与强盗”，由贪污犯按照相同的规则和相同的回报进行游戏；“海关与强盗”，由走私犯进行游戏等等。特别值得关注的是“法庭”的犯罪变体。尽管专业人士采取了各种预防措施，但有时仍可能被捕并接受审判。对他而言，“法庭”是一种程序，他按照法律顾问的指示执行。而对于律师来说，如果他们是那种执着于胜利的人，“法庭”本质上是一场与陪审团进行的游戏，其目标是赢而不是输，而这被社会上的很大一部分人视为一种建设性的游戏。

Antithesis. This is the concern of qualified criminologists rather than psychiatrists. The police and judiciary apparatus are not antithetical, but are playing their roles in the game under the rules set up by society.

对立关系。这应该是专业犯罪学家而非精神病学家关注的问题。警察和司法机构并非对立的，而是在社会制定的规则下各自扮演着自己的角色。

One thing should be emphasized, however. Research workers in criminology may joke that some criminals behave as though they enjoyed the chase and wanted to be caught, or they may read the idea and agree in a deferential way. But they show little tendency to consider such an ‘academic’ factor as decisive in their ‘serious’ work. For one thing, there is no way to unmask this element through the standard methods of psychological research. The investigator must therefore either overlook a crucial point because he cannot work it with his research tools, or else change his tools. The fact is that those tools have so far not yielded one single solution to any problem in criminology. Researchers might therefore be better off discarding the old methods and tackling the problem freshly. Until C & R is accepted not merely as an interesting anomaly, but as the very heart of the matter in a significant percentage of cases, much research in criminology will continue to deal with trivialities, doctrines, peripheral issues or irrelevancies. 1

然而，有一点需要强调。犯罪学研究人员可能会开玩笑说，有些罪犯的行为就像享受追逐的过程，渴望被抓；或者他们可能会读到这种观点，并表示赞同。但他们很少会将这种“学术”因素视为其“严肃”工作中的决定性因素。首先，心理学研究的标准方法根本无法揭示这一因素。因此，研究者要么因为无法运用现有研究工具而忽略关键点，要么就得更换研究工具。事实上，这些工具迄今为止尚未为犯罪学中的任何问题提供任何单一的解决方案。因此，研究人员或许应该摒弃旧方法，以全新的视角来审视这个问题。除非人们接受“犯罪与反应”（C&R）并非仅仅将其视为一种有趣的异常现象，而是将其视为相当一部分案件的核心所在，否则犯罪学领域的许多研究仍将继续纠缠于琐事、教条、边缘问题或无关紧要的细节。

ANALYSIS

分析

Thesis: See if you can catch me.

论文题目：看看你能不能抓住我。

Aim: Reassurance.

目的：安抚人心。

Roles: Robber , Cop (Judge).

角色：劫匪、警察（法官）。

Dynamics: Phallic intrusion, e.g., (1) Hide-and-seek, tag. (2) Crime.

动态：阳具入侵，例如，（1）捉迷藏、追逐游戏。（2）犯罪。

Social Paradigm: Parent-Child.

社会范式：亲子关系。

Child: ‘See if you can catch me.’

孩子：“看看你能不能抓住我。”

Parent: ‘That’s my job.’

家长：“那是我的工作。”

Psychological Paradigm: Parent-Child.

心理学范式：亲子关系。

Child: ‘You must catch me.’

孩子：“你一定要抓住我。”

Parent: ‘Aha, there you are.’

家长：“啊哈，你在这儿。”

Moves: (1) W: Defiance. B: Indignation. (2) W: Concealment. B: Frustration. (3) W: Provocation. B: Victory.

行动：（1）W：反抗。B：愤慨。（2）W：隐瞒。B：沮丧。（3）W：挑衅。B：胜利。

Advantages: (1) Internal Psychological – material indemnification for old wrong. (2) External Psychological – counterphobic. (3) Internal Social– See if you can catch me. (4) External Social –I almost got away with it (Pastime: They almost got away with it.) (5) Biological – notoriety. (6) Existential: I’ve always been a loser.

优势：（1）内部心理——对过去错误进行物质补偿。（2）外部心理——消除恐惧。（3）内部社会——看看你们能不能抓住我。（4）外部社会——我差点就逃脱了。（过去式：他们差点就逃脱了。）（5）生理——声名狼藉。（6）存在主义：我一直是个失败者。

2 · HOW DO YOU GET OUT OF HERE

2. 你该如何离开这里？

Thesis. The historical evidence is that those prisoners survive best who have their time structured by an activity, pastime or a game. This is apparently well known to political police, who are said to break some prisoners down simply by keeping them inactive and in a state of social deprivation.

论点：历史证据表明，那些时间安排得当，例如有某种活动、消遣或游戏的囚犯，生存得最好。政治警察显然深谙此道，据说他们仅仅通过让囚犯保持无所事事、与世隔绝的状态，就能摧毁一些囚犯的意志。

The favoured activity of solitary prisoners is reading or writing books, and the favoured pastime is escape, some of whose practitioners, such as Casanova and Baron Trenck, have become famous.

单独监禁的囚犯最喜欢的活动是读书或写作，最喜欢的消遣是越狱，其中一些越狱者，如卡萨诺瓦和特伦克男爵，已经名声大噪。

The favoured game is ‘How Do You Get Out of Here?’ (‘Want Out’), which may also be played in state hospitals. It must be distinguished from the operation (see page 44 ) of the same name, known as ‘Good Behaviour’. An inmate who really wants to be free will find out how to comply with the authorities so as to be released at the earliest possible moment. Nowadays this may often be accomplished by playing a good game of ‘Psychiatry’, Group Therapy Type. The game of ‘Want Out’, however, is played by inmates or by patients whose Child does not want to get out. They simulate ‘Good Behaviour’, but at the critical point they sabotage themselves so as not to be released. Thus in ‘Good Behaviour’ Parent, Adult and Child work together to be discharged; in ‘Want Out’ Parent and Adult go through the prescribed motions until the critical moment, when the Child, who is actually frightened at the prospect of venturing into the uncertain world, takes over and spoils the effect. ‘Want Out’ was common in the late 1930s among recently arrived immigrants from Germany who became psychotic. They would improve and beg for release from the hospital; but as the day of liberation approached, their psychotic manifestations would recur.

最受欢迎的游戏是“如何离开这里？”（简称“想出去”），这种游戏在州立医院里也可能玩。它必须与同名的“良好行为”（参见第44页）区分开来。真正想获得自由的囚犯会想方设法遵守当局的规矩，以便尽早获释。如今，这通常可以通过玩好“精神病学”游戏（团体治疗类型）来实现。然而，“想出去”游戏是由囚犯或孩子不想出院的病人玩的。他们假装“良好行为”，但在关键时刻却会自毁前程，以免被释放。因此，在“良好行为”中，父母、成人和孩子共同努力出院；而在“想出去”中，父母和成人按部就班地进行，直到关键时刻，孩子——实际上害怕冒险进入未知的世界——接管了局面，破坏了整个过程。 20世纪30年代末，许多刚从德国抵达美国的移民出现精神病症状，其中“想要出院”的现象十分普遍。他们的病情会好转，并恳求出院；但随着获释日期的临近，他们的精神病症状又会复发。

Antithesis. Both ‘Good Behaviour’ and ‘Want Out’ are recognized by alert administrators and can be dealt with at the executive level. Beginners in group therapy, however, are often taken in. A competent group therapist, knowing these are the most frequent manipulations in psychiatrically oriented prisons, will be watching for them and will ferret them out at an early phase. Since ‘Good Behaviour’ is an honest operation, it may be treated as such, and there is no harm in discussing it openly. ‘Want Out’, on the other hand, requires active therapy if the frightened inmate is to be rehabilitated.

对立面。“良好行为”和“想要退出”都能被警觉的管理者识别出来，并可在管理层层面加以处理。然而，团体治疗的初学者往往会被蒙蔽。一位称职的团体治疗师深知这些是精神病监狱中最常见的操纵手段，因此会密切关注并及早发现。由于“良好行为”是一种诚实的行为，因此可以将其视为诚实的行为，公开讨论也无妨。另一方面，如果想要帮助受惊的囚犯改过自新，“想要退出”则需要积极的治疗。

Relatives. A close relative of ‘Want Out’ is an operation called ‘You’ve Got to Listen’. Here the inmate of an institution or the client of a social agency demands the right to make complaints. The complaints are often irrelevant. His main purpose is to assure himself that he will be listened to by the authorities. If they make the mistake of thinking that he expects the complaints to be acted on and cut him off as too demanding, there may be trouble. If they accede to his demands, he will increase them. If they merely listen patiently and with signs of interest, the ‘You’ve Got to Listen’ player will be satisfied and cooperative, and will not ask for anything more. The administrator must learn to distinguish ‘You’ve Got to Listen’ from serious demands for remedial action. 2

亲属。“想出去”的近亲是“你必须听我说”这种做法。在这种做法中，机构中的被收容者或社会服务机构的服务对象会要求获得投诉的权利。这些投诉往往无关紧要。他的主要目的是确保当局会倾听他的声音。如果当局误以为他期望投诉得到处理，并认为他要求过多而拒绝他，可能会出现问题。如果当局满足了他的要求，他就会提出更多要求。如果当局只是耐心倾听并表现出兴趣，“你必须听我说”的参与者就会感到满意并配合，不会再提出任何要求。管理者必须学会区分“你必须听我说”和真正需要采取补救措施的要求。

‘Bum Rap’ is another game that belongs in this family. A straight criminal may holler ‘Bum Rap’ in a real effort to get out, in which case it is part of the procedure. The inmate who plays ‘Bum Rap’ as a game, however, does not use it effectively to try to get out, since if he gets out he will no longer have much excuse to holler.

“冤案”是另一个属于此类游戏的。一个真正的罪犯可能会为了逃脱牢狱之灾而大喊“冤案”，在这种情况下，这本身就是监狱程序的一部分。然而，把“冤案”当成游戏来玩的囚犯，并不能有效地利用它来逃脱牢狱之灾，因为如果他真的逃脱了，他就没什么借口再喊了。

3 · LET’S PULL A FAST ONE ON JOEY

3. 让我们捉弄一下乔伊

Thesis . The prototype of this game is ‘The Big Store’, the big-time confidence game, but many small grifts and even the badger game are FOOJY. No man can be beaten at FOOJY unless he has larceny in his veins, because the first move is for Black to tell White that dumb-honest-old-Joey is just waiting to be taken. If White were completely honest, he would either back off or warn Joey, but he doesn’t. Just as Joey is about to pay off, something goes wrong, and White finds that his investment is gone. Or in the badger game, just as Joey is about to be cuckolded, he happens to walk in. Then White, who was playing his own rules in his own honest way, finds that he has to play Joey’s rules, and they hurt.

论点：这种游戏的原型是“大商店”，一种大型的诈骗游戏，但许多小型骗局，甚至獾游戏，都属于FOOJY的范畴。除非天生就具有盗窃本能，否则没人能在FOOJY中获胜，因为第一步是黑方告诉白方，傻乎乎却诚实的老乔伊正等着上当受骗。如果白方真的诚实，他要么会退缩，要么会警告乔伊，但他没有。就在乔伊即将付款的时候，出了点岔子，白方发现自己的投资打了水漂。或者在獾游戏中，就在乔伊即将被戴绿帽的时候，他碰巧走了进来。然后，原本按照自己的规则和诚实的方式行事的白方，发现自己不得不按照乔伊的规则行事，这让他很受伤。

Curiously enough, the mark is supposed to know the rules of FOOJY and stick to them. Honest squawking is a calculated risk of the con mob; they will not hold that against White, and he is even allowed a certain latitude in lying to the police to save his face. But if he goes too far and accuses them falsely of burglary, for example, that is cheating, and they resent it. On the other hand, there is little sympathy for a con man who gets into trouble by working a mark who is drunk, since this is improper procedure, and he should know better. The same applies if he is stupid enough to pick a mark with a sense of humour, since it is well known that such people cannot be trusted to play the straight man in FOOJY all the way down the line through the terminal game of ‘Cops and Robbers’. Experienced con men are scared of marks who laugh after they have been taken.

奇怪的是，被骗者必须了解并遵守FOOJY的规则。诚实地提醒他们，骗子团伙会承担一定的风险；他们不会因此责怪怀特，甚至允许他为了保全面子而对警察撒谎。但如果他做得太过分，比如诬告他们入室盗窃，那就是欺骗，他们会很生气。另一方面，如果骗子因为欺骗醉酒的被骗者而惹上麻烦，人们不会同情他，因为这不符合规定，他应该更懂事。如果他愚蠢到选择一个有幽默感的被骗者，情况也一样，因为众所周知，这种人不能被信任，无法在FOOJY游戏中扮演严肃的角色，直到最后变成“警察抓小偷”的游戏。经验丰富的骗子害怕那些上当后还笑着的被骗者。

It should be noted that a practical joke is not a game of FOOJY, because in a practical joke Joey is the one who suffers, while in FOOJY Joey comes out on top, and White is the one who suffers. A practical joke is a pastime, while FOOJY is a game in which the joke is arranged to backfire.

需要注意的是，恶作剧和FOOJY游戏并不相同，因为在恶作剧中，受害的是Joey，而在FOOJY游戏中，Joey反而是赢家，White才是受害方。恶作剧是一种消遣，而FOOJY则是一种故意设计成反噬的游戏。

It is evident that FOOJY is a three- or four-handed game, with the police playing the fourth hand, and that it is related to ‘Let’s You and Him Fight’.

很明显，FOOJY 是一种三人或四人游戏，警察玩第四手，而且它与“让你和他打一架”有关。

NOTE

笔记

Thanks are due to Dr Franklin Ernst of the California Medical Faculty at Vacavilie, Mr William Collins of the California Rehabilitation Center at Norco, and Mr Laurence Means of the California Institution for Men at Tehachapi, for their continued interest in studying the game of ‘Cops and Robbers’ and for their helpful discussions and criticisms.

感谢加州瓦卡维利医学院的富兰克林·恩斯特博士、加州诺科康复中心的威廉·柯林斯先生以及加州特哈查比男子监狱的劳伦斯·米恩斯先生，感谢他们对研究“警察与强盗”游戏的持续兴趣，以及他们提供的有益讨论和批评。

REFERENCES

参考

1. Frederick Wiseman, in ‘Psychiatry and the Law: Use and Abuse of Psychiatry in a Murder Case’ ( American Journal of Psychiatry, 118:289–299, 1961) gives a clear and tragic example of a hard form of ‘Cops and Robbers’. It concerns a 23-year-old-man who shot his fiancée and then turned himself in. This was not easy to arrange, since the police did not believe his story until he had repeated it four times. Later, he said: ‘It just seemed to me that all my life I was bound to end up in the chair. If that was the way it was, that was the way it would be.’ The author says it was farcical to expect a lay jury to understand the complex psychiatric testimony that was offered at the trial in technical jargon. In game terms, the central issue can be stated in words of no more than two syllables: A nine-year-old boy decides (for reasons clearly brought out at the trial) that he is bound to end up in the chair. He spends the rest of his life headed toward this goal, and using his girl friend as a target, in the end he sets himself up.

1. 弗雷德里克·怀斯曼在《精神病学与法律：谋杀案中精神病学的运用与滥用》（《美国精神病学杂志》，118:289–299，1961）一文中，清晰而悲惨地展现了一个硬核版的“警察抓小偷”案例。故事的主人公是一位23岁的男子，他枪杀了未婚妻后自首。这并非易事，因为警方直到他重复了四遍才相信他的说法。后来，他说：“我感觉自己这辈子注定要坐上电椅。如果命中注定如此，那就这样吧。” 作者指出，指望非专业陪审团理解庭审中用晦涩难懂的专业精神病学证词，简直是荒谬至极。用游戏术语来说，核心问题可以用不超过两个音节的词语概括：一个九岁男孩（在审判中已明确阐述其原因）认定自己注定要坐上电椅。他余生都朝着这个目标努力，并以女友为目标，最终却自食其果。

2. For further information about ‘Cops and Robbers’ and games played by prison inmates, see: Ernst, F. H., and Keating, W. C., ‘Psychiatric Treatment of the California Felon’, American Journal of Psychiatry, 120:974–979, 1964.

2. 有关“警察与强盗”游戏和监狱囚犯所玩游戏的更多信息，请参阅：Ernst, F. H. 和 Keating, W. C.，“加州重罪犯的精神病治疗”，《美国精神病学杂志》，120:974–979，1964 年。

#↩

11 · Consulting Room Games

11 · 咨询室游戏

G AMES that are tenaciously played in the therapeutic situation are the most important ones for the professional game analyst to be aware of. They can be most readily studied first hand in the consulting room. There are three types, according to the role of the agent:

在治疗情境中，那些被反复使用的游戏是专业游戏分析师最需要了解的游戏类型。在咨询室中，这些游戏类型最容易通过直接观察来研究。根据参与者的角色，这些游戏类型可分为三种：

1. Games played by therapists and case workers: ‘I’m Only Trying to Help You’ and ‘Psychiatry’.

1. 治疗师和个案工作者玩的游戏：“我只是想帮助你”和“精神病学”。

2. Games played by professionally trained people who are patients in therapy groups, such as ‘Greenhouse’.

2. 由受过专业训练的患者在治疗小组中玩的游戏，例如“温室”。

3. Games played by lay patients and clients: ‘Indigent’, ‘Peasant’, ‘Stupid’ and ‘Wooden Leg’.

3. 普通病人和顾客玩的游戏：“穷人”、“农民”、“笨蛋”和“木腿”。

1 · GREENHOUSE

1 · 温室

Thesis. This is a variation of ‘Psychiatry’, which is played hardest by young social scientists, such as clinical psychologists. In the company of their colleagues these young people tend to play ‘Psychoanalysis’, often in a jocular way, using such expressions as ‘Your hostility is showing’ or ‘How mechanical can a defence mechanism get ?’ This is usually a harmless and enjoyable pastime; it is a normal phase of their learning experience, and with a few originals in the group it can become quite amusing. (This writer’s preference is, ‘I see National Parapraxis Week is here again.’) As patients in psychotherapy groups some of these people are apt to indulge in this mutual critique more seriously; but since it is not highly productive in that situation, it may have to be headed off by the therapist. The proceedings may then turn into a game of ‘Greenhouse’.

论文。这是“精神病学”的一种变体，尤其受到年轻的社会科学家，例如临床心理学家的喜爱。在同事的陪伴下，这些年轻人常常玩“精神分析”游戏，通常以玩笑的方式进行，使用诸如“你的敌意暴露无遗”或“防御机制能有多机械？”之类的表达。这通常是一种无害且令人愉快的消遣；这是他们学习经历中的一个正常阶段，如果小组里有几个特立独行的人，游戏就会变得非常有趣。（笔者更喜欢用“看来全国口误周又来了。”）作为心理治疗小组的病人，这些人中的一些人可能会更认真地参与这种相互批评；但由于在这种情况下这种批评效率不高，治疗师可能需要介入制止。这时，治疗过程可能会变成一场“温室”游戏。

There is a strong tendency for recent graduates to have an exaggerated respect for what they call ‘Genuine Feelings’. The expression of such a feeling may be preceded by an announcement that it is on its way. After the announcement, the feeling is described, or rather presented before the group, as though it were a rare flower which should be regarded with awe. The reactions of the other members are received very solemnly, and they take on the air of connoisseurs at a botanical garden. The problem seems to be, in the jargon of game analysis, whether this one is good enough to be exhibited in the National Feeling Show. A questioning intervention by the therapist may be strongly resented, as though he were some clumsy-fingered clod mauling the fragile petals of an exotic century plant. The therapist, naturally, feels that in order to understand the anatomy and physiology of a flower, it may be necessary to dissect it.

应届毕业生往往对他们所谓的“真情实感”抱有过分的敬意。表达这种感受之前，他们可能会先宣布即将表达。宣布之后，这种感受会被描述，或者更确切地说，是呈现在众人面前，仿佛它是一朵珍稀花卉，值得敬畏。其他成员的反应也显得异常严肃，仿佛他们是植物园里的鉴赏家。问题似乎在于，用游戏分析的术语来说，这种感受是否足够优秀，可以参加全国情感展。治疗师的提问可能会遭到强烈的反感，仿佛他是一个笨手笨脚的家伙，正在粗暴地对待一株珍稀的龙舌兰的花瓣。治疗师自然而然地认为，为了了解一朵花的解剖结构和生理机能，或许有必要对其进行解剖。

Antithesis. The antithesis, which is crucial for therapeutic progress, is the irony of the above description. If this game is allowed to proceed, it may go on unchanged for years, after which the patient may feel that he has had a ‘therapeutic experience’ during which he has ‘expressed hostility’ and learned to ‘face feelings’ in a way which gives him an advantage over less fortunate colleagues. Meanwhile very little of dynamic significance may have happened, and certainly the investment of time has not been used to maximum therapeutic advantage.

对立面。对立面对于治疗进展至关重要，它正是上述描述的讽刺之处。如果任由这种游戏继续下去，它可能多年不变，之后患者可能会觉得自己经历了一次“治疗体验”，在此期间他“表达了敌意”，并学会了“面对情绪”，从而使他比其他不幸的同伴更有优势。与此同时，可能几乎没有发生任何具有动态意义的事情，而且投入的时间也肯定没有得到最大的治疗效益。

The irony in the initial description is directed not against the patients but against their teachers and the cultural milieu which encourages such over-fastidiousness. If properly timed, a sceptical remark may successfully divorce them from foppish Parental influences and lead to a less self-conscious robustness in their transactions with each other. Instead of cultivating feelings in a kind of hothouse atmosphere, they may just let them grow naturally, to be plucked when they are ripe.

最初描述中的讽刺并非针对患者，而是针对他们的老师以及助长这种过分讲究的文化环境。如果时机恰当，一句质疑的评论或许能成功地让他们摆脱父母浮夸的影响，并在彼此交往中展现出一种不那么拘谨的自信。与其在温室般的环境中精心培育情感，不如让它们自然生长，待其成熟后再采摘。

The most obvious advantage of this game is the external psychological, since it avoids intimacy by setting up special conditions under which feelings may be expressed, and special restrictions on the responses of those present.

这款游戏最明显的优势在于其外部心理效应，因为它通过设定特殊的条件来表达情感，并对在场者的反应施加特殊的限制，从而避免了亲密关系。

2 · I’M ONLY TRYING TO HELP YOU

2. 我只是想帮你

Thesis. This game may be played in any professional situation and is not confined to psychotherapists and welfare workers. However, it is found most commonly and in its most florid form among social workers with a certain type of training. The analysis of this game was clarified for the writer under curious circumstances. All the players at a poker game had folded except two, a research psychologist and a businessman. The businessman, who had a high hand, bet; the psychologist, who had an unbeatable one, raised. The businessman looked puzzled, whereupon the psychologist remarked facetiously: ‘Don’t be upset, I’m only trying to help you!’ The businessman hesitated, and finally put in his chips. The psychologist showed the winning hand, whereupon the other threw down his cards in disgust. The others present then felt free to laugh at the psychologist’s joke, and the loser remarked ruefully: ‘You sure were helpful!’ The psychologist cast a knowing glance at the writer, implying that the joke had really been made at the expense of the psychiatric profession. It was at that moment that the structure of this game became clear.

论点：这种游戏可以在任何专业场合进行，并非仅限于心理治疗师和福利工作者。然而，它在接受过特定类型培训的社会工作者中最常见，也表现得最为活跃。笔者是在一次奇特的情境下对这种游戏有了更清晰的认识。在一场扑克游戏中，除了两位玩家——一位研究心理学家和一位商人——之外，其他玩家都弃牌了。商人手牌很大，于是下注；心理学家手牌无敌，于是加注。商人一脸疑惑，心理学家便开玩笑地说：“别生气，我只是想帮你！”商人犹豫了一下，最终还是下了筹码。心理学家亮出了赢牌，商人见状，厌恶地扔掉了手中的牌。在场的其他人随即都放声大笑，嘲笑心理学家的玩笑，而输家则懊恼地说道：“你真是帮了大忙啊！”心理学家意味深长地看了写信人一眼，暗示这个玩笑实际上是在嘲讽精神病学界。就在那一刻，这个游戏的规则才真正清晰起来。

The worker or therapist, of whatever profession, gives some advice to a client or patient. The patient returns and reports that the suggestion did not have the desired effect. The worker shrugs off this failure with a feeling of resignation, and tries again. If he is more watchful, he may detect at this point a twinge of frustration, but he will try again anyway. Usually he feels little need to question his own motives, because he knows that many of his similarly trained colleagues do the same thing, and that he is following the ‘correct’ procedure and will receive full support from his supervisors.

无论从事何种职业，工作人员或治疗师都会给来访者或患者一些建议。患者回来后反映建议没有达到预期效果。工作人员对此感到无奈，耸耸肩，然后再次尝试。如果他更细心一些，或许会察觉到此时自己略带沮丧，但他仍然会继续尝试。通常，他很少会质疑自己的动机，因为他知道许多受过类似培训的同事也会这样做，而且他认为自己遵循的是“正确”的流程，并且会得到主管的全力支持。

If he runs up against a hard player, such as a hostile obsessional, he will find it more and more difficult to avoid feeling inadequate. Then he is in trouble, and the situation will slowly deteriorate. In the worst case, he may come up against an angry paranoid who will rush in one day in a rage, crying:‘Look what you made me do!’ Then his frustration will come strongly to the fore in the spoken or unspoken thought: ‘But I was only trying to help you!’ His bewilderment at the ingratitude may cause him considerable suffering, indicating the complex motives underlying his own behaviour. This bewilderment is the payoff.

如果他遇到难缠的对手，比如一个充满敌意的强迫症患者，他会越来越难以摆脱自卑感。这时他就麻烦了，情况会逐渐恶化。最糟糕的情况是，他可能会遇到一个愤怒的偏执狂，对方某天会怒气冲冲地闯进来，大喊：“看看你都把我逼成什么样了！”这时，他的挫败感会强烈地涌上心头，他会在心里或说出来或没说出口地想：“但我只是想帮你啊！”这种忘恩负义让他感到困惑，可能会给他带来巨大的痛苦，也暗示着他自身行为背后复杂的动机。而这种困惑，正是他努力的回报。

Legitimate helpers should not be confused with people who play ‘I’m Only Trying to Help You’ (ITHY). ‘I think we can do something about it’, ‘I know what to do’, ‘I was assigned to help you’ or ‘My fee for helping you will be..’ are different from ‘I’m only trying to help you’. The first four, in good faith, represent Adult offers to put professional qualifications at the disposal of the distressed patient or client; ITHY has an ulterior motive which is more important than professional skill in determining the out come. This motive is based on the position that people are ungrateful and disappointing. The prospect of success is alarming to the Parent of the professional and is an invitation to sabotage, because success would threaten the position. The ITHY player needs to be reassured that help will not be accepted no matter how strenuously it is offered. The client responds with ‘Look How Hard I’m Trying’ or ‘There’s Nothing You Can Do to Help Me’. More flexible players can compromise: it is all right for people to accept help providing it takes them a long time to do so. Hence therapists tend to feel apologetic for a quick result, since they know that some of their colleagues at staff meetings will be critical. At the opposite pole from hard ITHY players, such as are found among social workers, are good lawyers who help their clients without personal involvement or sentimentality. Here craftsmanship takes the place of covert strenuousness.

真正的帮助者不应与那些扮演“我只是想帮你”（ITHY）角色的人混淆。“我觉得我们可以做点什么”、“我知道该怎么做”、“我被指派来帮助你”或“我帮你的费用是……”与“我只是想帮你”截然不同。前四句话出于善意，代表着成年人愿意运用其专业资质帮助陷入困境的患者或客户；而“我只是想帮你”则另有图谋，其目的远比专业技能更重要。这种目的源于一种根深蒂固的观念：人们忘恩负义、令人失望。成功的前景令专业人士的“家长”感到不安，并诱使他们进行破坏，因为成功会威胁到他们的地位。扮演“我只是想帮你”角色的人需要被反复告知，无论他们多么努力地提供帮助，都不会被接受。客户会回应说：“你看我多么努力啊”或“你帮不了我”。更灵活的从业者能够做出妥协：人们接受帮助是可以接受的，只要这个过程需要很长时间。因此，治疗师往往会因为快速见效而感到抱歉，因为他们知道在员工会议上，一些同事会提出批评。与那些强硬的、唯我独尊的从业者（例如社工）截然相反的是优秀的律师，他们帮助客户时不带个人情感或个人偏见。在这里，精湛的技艺取代了隐秘的努力。

Some schools of social work seem to be primarily academies for the training of professional ITHY players, and it is not easy for their graduates to desist from playing it. An example which may help to illustrate some of the foregoing points will be found in the description of the complementary game ‘Indigence’.

一些社会工作学院似乎主要致力于培养专业的“ITHY”玩家，其毕业生很难放弃这款游戏。以下对配套游戏“贫困”的描述或许能更好地说明上述观点。

ITHY and its variants are easy to find in everyday life. It is played by family friends and relatives (e.g., ‘I Can Get It For You Wholesale’), and by adults who do community work with children. It is a favourite among parents, and the complementary game played by the offspring is usually ‘Look What You Made Me Do’. Socially it may be a variant of ‘Schlemiel’ in which the damage is done while being helpful rather than impulsively; here the client is represented by a victim who may be playing ‘Why Does This Always Happen To Me?’ or one of its variants.

“我帮你搞定一切”（ITHY）及其变体在日常生活中随处可见。家人朋友和亲戚之间会玩（例如，“我能帮你批发”），从事儿童社区工作的成年人也会玩。它深受父母喜爱，孩子们通常会玩“看看你都做了些什么”（Look What You Made Me Do）。在社交场合，它可能是“笨蛋”（Schlemiel）游戏的一种变体，只不过造成伤害的并非出于冲动，而是出于好心；在这种情况下，当事人扮演的是受害者，他可能正在玩“为什么这种事总是发生在我身上？”（Why Does This Always Happen To Me?）或其变体游戏。

Antithesis. There are several devices available for the professional to handle an invitation to play this game, and his selection will depend on the state of the relationship between himself and the patient, particularly on the attitude of the patient’s Child.

对比。专业人士可以使用多种方法来应对参与这种游戏的邀请，其选择将取决于他与患者之间的关系状态，尤其是患者孩子的态度。

1. The classical psychoanalytic antithesis is the most thoroughgoing and the most difficult for the patient to tolerate. The invitation is completely ignored. The patient then tries harder and harder. Eventually he falls into a state of despair, manifested by anger or depression, which is the characteristic sign that a game has been frustrated. This situation may lead to a useful confrontation.

1. 经典的精神分析对立是最彻底的，也是患者最难忍受的。患者完全无视这种邀请，反而更加努力地尝试。最终，他陷入绝望，表现为愤怒或抑郁，这是游戏受挫的典型表现。这种情况可能会促成一次有益的对抗。

2. A more gentle (but not prim) confrontation may be attempted on the first invitation. The therapist states that he is the patient’s therapist and not his manager.

2. 在第一次被问及时，可以尝试用更温和（但并非生硬）的方式进行沟通。治疗师要表明自己是患者的治疗师，而不是患者的管理者。

3. An even more gentle procedure is to introduce the patient into a therapy group, and let the other patients handle it.

3. 更温和的方法是让患者加入治疗小组，让其他患者来处理。

4. With an acutely disturbed patient it may be necessary to play along during the initial phase. These patients should be treated by a psychiatrist, who being a medical man, can prescribe both medications and some of the hygienic measures which are still valuable, even in this day of tranquillizers, in the treatment of such people. If the physician prescribes a hygienic regimen, which may include baths, exercise, rest periods, and regular meals along with medication, the patient (1) carries out the regimen and feels better (2) carries out the regimen scrupulously and complains that it does not help; (3) mentions casually that he forgot to carry out the instructions or that he has abandoned the regimen because it was not doing any good. In the second and third case it is then up to the psychiatrist to decide whether the patient is amenable to game analysis at that point, or whether some other form of treatment is indicated to prepare him for later psychotherapy. The relationship between the adequacy of the regimen and the patient’s tendency to play games with it should be carefully evaluated by the psychiatrist before he decides how to proceed next.

4. 对于病情危重的患者，在初期阶段可能需要配合治疗。这类患者应由精神科医生诊治。精神科医生作为医生，可以开具药物和一些卫生措施，即使在如今镇静剂盛行的时代，这些措施对这类患者的治疗仍然有效。如果医生开具了包括沐浴、运动、休息和规律饮食在内的卫生方案，并配合药物治疗，患者可能会出现以下三种情况：(1) 严格执行方案并感觉好转；(2) 一丝不苟地执行方案，但抱怨没有效果；(3) 漫不经心地提到自己忘记执行医嘱，或者因为方案无效而放弃了。在第二种和第三种情况下，精神科医生需要判断患者此时是否适合接受游戏分析，或者是否需要其他形式的治疗来为后续的心理治疗做好准备。精神科医生在决定下一步治疗方案之前，应该仔细评估治疗方案的充分性与患者玩弄治疗方案的倾向之间的关系。

For the patient, on the other hand, the antithesis is, ‘Don’t tell me what to do to help myself, I’ll tell you what to do to help me.’ If the therapist is known to be a Schlemiel, the correct antithesis for the patient to use is, ‘Don’t help me, help him.’ But serious players of ‘I’m Only Trying to Help You’ are generally lacking in a sense of humour. Antithetical moves on the part of a patient are usually unfavourably received, and may result in the therapist’s lifelong enmity. In everyday life such moves should not be initiated unless one is prepared to carry them through ruthlessly and take the consequences. For example, spurning a relative who ‘Can Get It For You Wholesale’ may cause serious domestic complications.

另一方面，对病人而言，反义词是：“别告诉我该怎么做才能自助，我会告诉你该怎么做才能帮到我。”如果治疗师是个出了名的笨蛋，病人应该用的反义词是：“别帮我，去帮他。”但那些一本正经地说“我只是想帮你”的人通常缺乏幽默感。病人采取反义词的做法通常会遭到反驳，甚至可能导致治疗师终生不和。在日常生活中，除非做好了毫不留情地执行并承担后果的准备，否则不应该采取这种做法。例如，拒绝一个“能帮你搞到一切”的亲戚可能会引发严重的家庭矛盾。

ANALYSIS

分析

Thesis: Nobody ever does what I tell them.

论点：从来没有人听我的话。

Aim: Alleviation of guilt.

目的：减轻内疚感。

Roles: Helper , Client.

角色：帮助者、客户。

Dynamics: Masochism.

动力学：受虐倾向。

Examples: (1) Children learning, parent intervenes. (2) Social worker and client.

例如：（1）儿童学习，家长介入。（2）社工与服务对象。

Social Paradigm: Parent-Child.

社会范式：亲子关系。

Child: ‘What do I do now?’

孩子：“我现在该怎么办？”

Parent: ‘Here’s what you do.’

家长：“你应该这样做。”

Psychological Paradigm: Parent-Child.

心理学范式：亲子关系。

Parent: ‘See how adequate I am.’

家长：“看看我多么称职。”

Child: ‘I’ll make you feel inadequate.’

孩子：“我会让你觉得自己不够好。”

Moves: (1) Instructions requested – Instructions given. (2) Procedure bungled – Reproof. (3) Demonstration that procedures are faulty – Implicit apology.

行动步骤：（1）请求指示——给予指示。（2）程序出错——予以责备。（3）证明程序存在缺陷——含蓄道歉。

Advantages: (1) Internal Psychological – martyrdom. (2) External Psychological – avoids facing inadequacies. (3) Internal Social – ‘PTA’, Projective Type; ingratitude. (4) External Social – ‘Psychiatry’, Projective Type. (5) Biological – slapping from client, stroking from supervisors. (6) Existential – All people are ungrateful.

优势：（1）内在心理因素——自我牺牲。（2）外在心理因素——逃避面对自身不足。（3）内在社会因素——创伤后应激障碍（PTA），投射型人格；忘恩负义。（4）外在社会因素——精神病学，投射型人格。（5）生理因素——被客户掌掴，被上级抚摸。（6）存在主义因素——所有人都忘恩负义。

3 · INDIGENCE

3. 贫困

Thesis. The thesis of this game is best stated by Henry Miller in The Colossus of Maroussi: ‘The event must have taken place during the year when I was looking for a job without the slightest intention of taking one. It reminded me that, desperate as I thought myself to be, I had not even bothered to look through the columns of the want ads.’

主题。亨利·米勒在《马鲁西巨像》中对这款游戏的主题做了最好的阐述：“这件事肯定发生在我找工作却丝毫没有接受工作的那一年。它提醒我，尽管我自认为很绝望，但我甚至懒得翻阅招聘广告。”

This game is one of the complements of ‘I’m Only Trying to Help You’ (ITHY) as it is played by social workers who earn their living by it. ‘Indigence’ is played just as professionally by the client who earns his living in this manner. The writer’s own experience with ‘Indigence’ is limited, but the following account by one of his most accomplished students illustrates the nature of this game and its place in our society.

这个游戏是“我只是想帮你”（ITHY）的补充，因为社会工作者靠它谋生。“贫困”这个游戏同样被那些以此为生的客户专业地玩弄。笔者本人对“贫困”的了解有限，但他一位最优秀的学生的以下描述，生动地展现了这个游戏的本质及其在我们社会中的地位。

Miss Black was a social worker in a welfare agency whose avowed purpose, for which it received a government subsidy, was the economic rehabilitation of indigents – which in effect meant getting them to find and retain gainful employment. The clients of this agency were continually ‘making progress’, according to official reports, but very few of them were actually ‘rehabilitated’. This was understandable, it was claimed, because most of them had been welfare clients for several years, going from agency to agency and sometimes being involved with five or six agencies at a time, so that it was evident that they were ‘difficult cases’.

布莱克小姐是一家福利机构的社工，该机构的宗旨（也是其获得政府补贴的宗旨）是帮助贫困者实现经济康复——实际上就是帮助他们找到并保住有收入的工作。官方报告称，该机构的服务对象一直在“取得进步”，但真正“康复”的人却寥寥无几。有人声称，这可以理解，因为他们中的大多数人已经领取福利多年，辗转于各个机构之间，有时甚至同时与五六个机构打交道，显然他们是“疑难个案”。

Miss Black, from her training in game analysis, soon realized that the staff of her agency was playing a consistent game of ITH Y, and wondered how the clients were responding to this. In order to check, she asked her own clients from week to week how many job opportunities they had actually investigated. She was interested to discover that although they were theoretically supposed to be looking assiduously for work from day to day, actually they devoted very little effort to this, and sometimes the token efforts they did make had an ironic quality. For example, one man said that he answered at least one advertisement a day looking for work. ‘What kind of work?’ she inquired. He said he wanted to go into saleswork. ‘Is that the only kind of ad you answer?’ she asked. He said that it was, but it was too bad that he was a stutterer, as that held him back from his chosen career. About this time it came to the attention of her supervisor that she was asking these questions, and she was reprimanded for putting ‘undue pressure’ on her clients.

布莱克小姐凭借游戏分析方面的训练，很快意识到她所在机构的员工一直在玩“ITH Y”游戏，她想知道客户对此有何反应。为了验证这一点，她每周都会询问自己的客户，他们实际考察过多少工作机会。她惊讶地发现，尽管理论上他们应该每天勤奋找工作，但实际上他们在这方面投入的精力却很少，有时他们象征性的努力甚至带有讽刺意味。例如，一位男士说他每天至少会回复一则求职广告。“什么类型的工作？”她问道。他说他想从事销售工作。“你只回复这类广告吗？”她问。他说是的，但可惜的是他口吃，这阻碍了他从事自己选择的职业。就在这时，她的主管注意到了她问这些问题，并批评她给客户施加了“不当压力”。

Miss Black decided nevertheless to go ahead and rehabilitate some of them. She selected those who were able-bodied and did not seem to have a valid reason to continue to receive welfare funds. With this selected group, she talked over the games ITHY and ‘Indigence’. When they were willing to concede the point, she said that unless they found jobs she was going to cut them off from welfare funds and refer them to a different kind of agency. Several of them almost immediately found employment, some for the first time in years. But they were indignant at her attitude, and some of them wrote letters to her supervisor complaining about it. The supervisor called her in and reprimanded her even more severely on the ground that although her former clients were working, they were not ‘really rehabilitated’. The supervisor indicated that there was some question whether they would retain Miss Black in the agency. Miss Black, as much as she dared without further jeopardizing her position, tactfully tried to elicit what would constitute ‘really rehabilitated’ in the agency’s opinion. This was not clarified. She was only told that she was ‘putting undue pressure’ on people, and the fact that they were supporting their families for the first time in years was in no way to her credit.

尽管如此，布莱克小姐还是决定继续帮助他们中的一些人重返社会。她挑选了一些身体健全、似乎没有正当理由继续领取福利金的人。她和这些人一起玩了“ITHY”和“贫困”这两个游戏。当他们愿意承认这一点时，她告诉他们，除非他们找到工作，否则她将停止发放他们的福利金，并将他们转介到其他机构。他们中的一些人几乎立刻找到了工作，有些人甚至多年来第一次找到了工作。但他们对她的态度感到愤慨，有些人写信给她的主管投诉。主管把她叫去谈话，更加严厉地训斥了她，理由是虽然她以前的客户找到了工作，但他们并没有“真正重返社会”。主管暗示，他们可能会考虑是否继续聘用布莱克小姐。布莱克小姐在不进一步危及自己职位的前提下，尽可能地试探性地询问机构对“真正重返社会”的定义是什么。这一点并未得到澄清。她只被告知她“给人们施加了不必要的压力”，而这些人多年来第一次养家糊口的事实，丝毫没有让她感到值得称赞。

Because she needed her job and was now in danger of losing it, some of her friends tried to help. The respected head of a psychiatric clinic wrote to the supervisor, stating that he had heard Miss Black had done some particularly effective work with welfare clients, and asking whether she might discuss her findings at a staff conference at his clinic. The supervisor refused permission.

因为她需要这份工作，而且现在面临失业的危险，所以她的一些朋友试图帮助她。一位德高望重的精神科诊所主任写信给她的主管，说他听说布莱克小姐在帮助福利机构的客户方面做得非常出色，并询问她是否可以在诊所的员工会议上分享她的研究成果。主管拒绝了她的请求。

In this case the rules of ‘Indigent’ were set up by the agency to complement the local rules of ITHY. There was a tacit agreement between the worker and the client which read as follows:

在这种情况下，“贫困”的定义由中介机构制定，以补充ITHY的当地规定。工作人员和客户之间存在一项默契协议，内容如下：

W. ‘I’ll try to help you (providing you don’t get better).’

W：“我会尽力帮助你（前提是你的病情没有好转）。”

C. ‘I’ll look for employment (providing I don’t have to find any).

C.“我会去找工作（前提是我不需要找工作）。

If a client broke the agreement by getting better, the agency lost a client, and the client lost his welfare benefits, and both felt penalized. If a worker like Miss Black broke the agreement by making the client actually find work, the agency was penalized by the client’s complaints, which might come to the attention of higher authorities, while again the client lost his welfare benefits.

如果客户病情好转而违反协议，机构就会失去客户，客户也会失去福利金，双方都会感到受损。如果像布莱克小姐这样的工作人员让客户实际找到工作而违反协议，机构会因客户的投诉而受到惩罚，这些投诉可能会引起上级部门的注意，而客户同样会失去福利金。

As long as both obeyed the implicit rules, both got what they wanted. The client received his benefits and soon learned what the agency wanted in return: an opportunity to ‘reach out’ (as part of ITHY) plus ‘clinical material’ (to present at ‘client-centred’ staff conferences). The client was glad to comply with these demands, which gave him as much pleasure as it did the agency. Thus they got along well together, and neither felt any desire to terminate such a satisfying relationship. Miss Black, in effect, ‘reached in’ instead of ‘reaching out’, and proposed a ‘community-centred’ staff conference instead of a ‘client-centred’ one; and this disturbed all the others concerned in spite of the fact that she was thus only complying with the stated intent of the regulations.

只要双方都遵守不成文的规则，就能各取所需。客户获得了应有的权益，并很快明白了机构想要什么回报：一个“拓展人脉”（作为ITHY项目的一部分）的机会，以及“临床资料”（用于在“以客户为中心”的员工会议上进行展示）。客户乐于满足这些要求，这让他和机构都感到满意。因此，他们相处融洽，双方都不想结束这种令人满意的关系。布莱克小姐实际上是“介入”而非“拓展人脉”，她提议召开“以社区为中心”的员工会议，而不是“以客户为中心”的会议；尽管她这样做只是遵守了规定的既定意图，但这仍然引起了所有其他相关人员的不满。

Two things should be noted here. First, ‘Indigence’ as a game rather than a condition due to physical, mental, or economic disability, is played by only a limited percentage of welfare clients. Second, it will only be supported by social workers who are trained to play ITHY. It will not be well-tolerated by other workers.

这里有两点需要注意。首先，“贫困”作为一种游戏而非由身体、精神或经济残疾造成的状况，只有一小部分福利领取者会参与其中。其次，只有接受过“贫困即游戏”（ITHY）训练的社工才会支持这种游戏，其他社工很难接受。

Allied games are ‘Veteran’ and ‘Clinic’. ‘Veteran’ displays the same symbiotic relationship, this time between the Veterans Administration, allied organizations, and a certain number of ‘professional veterans’ who share the legitimate privileges of disabled ex-servicemen. ‘Clinic’ is played by a certain percentage of those who attend the out-patient departments of large hospitals. Unlike those who play ‘Indigent’ or ‘Veteran’, patients who play ‘Clinic’ do not receive financial remuneration, but get other advantages. They serve a useful social purpose, since they are willing to cooperate in the training of medical personnel and in studies of disease processes. From this they may get a legitimate Adult satisfaction not available to players of ‘Indigence’ and ‘Veteran’.

联盟游戏包括“老兵”和“诊所”。“老兵”展现了同样的共生关系，这次是退伍军人事务部、联盟组织和一定数量的“职业退伍军人”之间的共生关系，这些“职业退伍军人”享有残疾退伍军人的合法权益。“诊所”游戏则由一部分大型医院门诊部的患者参与。与参与“贫困”或“老兵”游戏的患者不同，“诊所”游戏的患者不获得经济报酬，但可以获得其他方面的益处。他们发挥着有益的社会作用，因为他们愿意参与医务人员的培训和疾病过程的研究。从中，他们可以获得“贫困”和“老兵”游戏玩家无法获得的合法成人满足感。

Antithesis. Antithesis, if indicated, consists in withholding the benefits. Here the risk is not primarily from the player himself, as in most other games, but from this game being culturally syntonic and fostered by the complementary ITHY players. The threat comes from professional colleagues and the aroused public, government agencies and protective unions. The complaints which follow an exhibition of anti-‘Indigence’ may lead to a loud outcry of ‘Yes, Yes, How About That?’ which may be regarded as a healthy, constructive operation or pastime, even if it occasionally discourages candidness. In fact, the whole American political system of democratic freedoms is based on a licence (not available under many other forms of government) to ask that question. Without such a licence, humanitarian social progress becomes seriously impeded.

对立。如果有必要，对立指的是剥夺利益。这里的风险主要并非来自玩家自身（如同大多数其他博弈），而是来自这种博弈在文化上是和谐的，并且是由与之互补的“ITHY”玩家所推动的。威胁来自专业同行、被激怒的公众、政府机构和保护性工会。在反“贫困”行为之后，随之而来的抱怨可能会引发“是啊，是啊，怎么样？”的强烈呼声，这可以被视为一种健康的、建设性的活动或消遣，即使它有时会阻碍坦诚。事实上，整个美国民主自由的政治体系都建立在一种（许多其他政体所不具备的）提出这个问题的许可之上。如果没有这种许可，人道主义社会进步将受到严重阻碍。

4 · PEASANT

4. 农民

Thesis. The prototype peasant is the arthritic Bulgarian villager who sells her only cow to raise money to go to the university clinic in Sofia. There the professor examines her and finds her case so interesting that he presents her in a clinical demonstration to the medical students. He outlines not only the pathology, symptoms and diagnosis, but also the treatment. This procedure fills her with awe. Before she leaves, the professor gives her a prescription and explains the treatment in more detail She is overcome with admiration for his learning and says the Bulgarian equivalent of, ‘Gee, you’re wonderful, Professor!’ However, she never has the prescription filled. First, there is no apothecary in her village; second, even if there were, she would never let such a valuable piece of paper out of her hands. Nor does she have the facilities for carrying out the rest of the treatment, such as diet, hydrotherapy and so on. She lives on, crippled as before, but happy now because she can tell everyone about the wonderful treatment prescribed for her by the great professor in Sofia, to whom she expresses her gratitude every night in her prayers.

论文。原型农妇是一位患有关节炎的保加利亚村民，她卖掉了自己唯一的一头牛，筹钱去索非亚的大学诊所就诊。在那里，一位教授为她做了检查，发现她的病情非常有趣，于是向医学生们做了临床演示。教授不仅讲解了病理、症状和诊断，还讲解了治疗方法。这个过程令她敬畏不已。临走前，教授给她开了处方，并更详细地解释了治疗方案。她被教授的学识深深折服，脱口而出“哇，教授，您太棒了！”（保加利亚语，意为“哇，您真了不起！”）。然而，她最终并没有去取药。首先，她的村子里没有药剂师；其次，即使有，她也绝不会轻易让如此珍贵的处方离开自己的手。此外，她也没有条件进行后续的治疗，例如饮食疗法、水疗等等。她虽然仍然活着，但和以前一样残疾，不过现在她很开心，因为她可以告诉所有人索非亚那位伟大的教授为她制定的奇妙治疗方案，她每晚都会在祈祷中向这位教授表达感激之情。

Years later, the Professor, in an unhappy frame of mind, happens to pass through the village on his way to see a wealthy but demanding patient. He remembers the peasant when she rushes out to kiss his hand and remind him of the marvellous regimen he put her on so long ago. He accepts her homage graciously, and is particularly gratified when she tells him how much good the treatment has done. In fact he is so carried away that he fails to notice that she limps as badly as ever.

多年后，教授心情郁闷，路过这个村庄，正要去探望一位富有但要求苛刻的病人。这时，那位农妇冲出来亲吻他的手，提醒他当年他为她制定的神奇疗法，教授这才想起了她。他欣然接受了她的敬意，尤其当她告诉他疗法效果显著时，他更是感到无比欣慰。事实上，他当时完全沉浸在喜悦之中，以至于没有注意到她走路一瘸一拐的程度和以前一样严重。

Socially ‘Peasant’ is played in an innocent and a dissembled form, both with the motto, ‘Gee you’re wonderful, Mr Murgatroyd!’ (GYWM). In the innocent form, Murgatroyd is wonderful. He is a celebrated poet, painter, philanthropist or scientist, and naïve young women frequently travel a long way in the hope of meeting him so that they can sit adoringly at his feet and romanticize his imperfections. A more sophisticated woman who sets out deliberately to have an affair or a marriage with such a man, whom she sincerely admires and appreciates, may be fully aware of his weaknesses. She may even exploit them in order to get what she wants. With these two types of women, the game arises from the romanticizing or exploiting of the imperfections, while the innocence lies in their genuine respect for his accomplishments, which they are able to evaluate correctly.

在社交游戏中，“平民”角色扮演有两种形式：一种是天真无邪的，另一种则是虚伪做作的，两种形式的共同点都是“哇，你真棒，默格特罗伊德先生！”（GYWM）。在天真无邪的版本中，默格特罗伊德先生是完美的。他是一位著名的诗人、画家、慈善家或科学家，天真的年轻女子常常远道而来，只为一睹他的风采，然后虔诚地拜倒在他的脚下，将他的缺点浪漫化。而一位更加世故的女性，如果刻意追求与这样一位她真心钦佩和欣赏的男士发展婚外情或步入婚姻殿堂，她可能完全了解他的弱点。她甚至会利用这些弱点来达到自己的目的。对于这两种类型的女性来说，游戏的乐趣在于对缺点的浪漫化或利用，而天真无邪则体现在她们对默格特罗伊德先生成就的真诚尊重，以及她们能够正确评价这些成就。

In the dissembled form, Murgatroyd may or may not be wonderful, but he comes up against a woman incapable of appreciating him in the best sense, in any case; perhaps she is a high-class prostitute. She plays ‘Little Old Me’ and uses GYWM as sheer flattery to attain her own ends. Underneath she is either bewildered by him or laughing at him. But she does not care about him; what she wants are the perquisites that go with him.

伪装下的默格特罗伊德或许才华横溢，或许平庸无奇，但他遇到的女人无论如何都无法真正欣赏他；或许她是一位高级妓女。她装出一副“小人物”的模样，利用GYWM的奉承来达到自己的目的。在她内心深处，她要么对他感到困惑，要么在嘲笑他。但她并不在意他这个人；她想要的只是与他相伴而来的各种好处。

Clinically ‘Peasant’ is played in two similar forms, with the motto, ‘Gee you’re wonderful, Professor!’ (GYWP). In the innocent form the patient may stay well as long as she can believe in GYWP, which places an obligation on the therapist to be well-behaved both in public and in private life. In the dissembled form the patient hopes the therapist will go along with her GYWP and think: ‘You’re uncommonly perceptive.’ (YUP). Once she has him in this position, she can make him look foolish and then move on to another therapist; if he cannot be so easily beguiled, he may actually be able to help her.

临床上，“农民”心理疗法有两种相似的形式，其核心信条都是“哇，教授，你真棒！”（GYWP）。在天真的形式中，只要病人相信GYWP，她就能保持健康，这就要求治疗师在公共和私下生活中都必须举止得体。在伪装的形式中，病人希望治疗师会认同她的GYWP，并认为：“你真是洞察力非凡。”（YUP）。一旦她让治疗师陷入这种状态，她就可以让他出丑，然后去找另一个治疗师；如果他不容易被蒙蔽，他或许真的能帮到她。

The simplest way for the patient to win GYWP is not to get better. If she is more malicious, she may take more positive steps to make the therapist look foolish. One woman played GYWP with her psychiatrist without any alleviations of symptoms; she finally left him with many salaams and apologies. She then went to her revered clergyman for help and played GYWP with him. After a few weeks she seduced him into a game of second degree ‘Rapo’. She then told her neighbour confidentially over the back fence how disappointed she was that so fine a man as Rev Black could, in a moment of weakness, make a pass at an innocent and unattractive woman like herself. Knowing his wife, she could forgive him, of course, but nevertheless, etc. This confidence just slipped out inadvertently, and it was only afterwards that she remembered ‘to her horror’ that the neighbour was an elder in the church. With her psychiatrist she won by not getting better; with her clergyman she won by seducing him, although she was reluctant to admit it. But a second psychiatrist introduced her to a therapy group where she could not manoeuvre as she had before. Then, with no GYWP and YUP to fill in her therapeutic time, she began to examine her behaviour more closely and with the help of the group was able to give up both her games – GYWP and ‘Rapo’.

对病人来说，赢得“善意游戏”（GYWP）最简单的方法就是病情没有好转。如果她心怀恶意，可能会采取更积极的措施来让治疗师出丑。一位女士和她的精神科医生玩“善意游戏”，但症状没有任何缓解；最后，她带着许多问候和歉意离开了医生。之后，她去找她尊敬的牧师寻求帮助，并和他玩起了“善意游戏”。几周后，她引诱牧师玩起了“拉波”（Rapo）游戏。然后，她隔着后院的篱笆，悄悄地告诉邻居，她多么失望，像布莱克牧师这样优秀的男人，竟然会在一时软弱的时候，对像她这样天真无邪、相貌平平的女人动手动脚。当然，她认识他的妻子，所以可以原谅他，但即便如此，等等。这些话只是无意中说出口的，事后她才“惊恐地”想起，邻居是教会的长老。和她的精神科医生玩“善意游戏”时，她赢了，因为她的病情没有好转。她通过勾引牧师赢得了他的芳心，尽管她不愿承认。但另一位精神科医生将她介绍到一个治疗小组，在那里她无法像以前那样玩弄权术。之后，由于没有了GYWP和YUP来打发治疗时间，她开始更仔细地审视自己的行为，并在小组的帮助下，最终戒掉了GYWP和“Rapo”这两个游戏。

Antithesis. The therapist must first decide whether the game is played innocently and hence should be allowed to continue for the benefit of the patient until her Adult is sufficiently well-established to risk countermeasures. If it is not innocent, the countermeasures may be taken at the first appropriate opportunity after the patient has been sufficiently well prepared so that she will be able to understand what happens. The therapist then steadfastly refuses to give advice, and when the patient begins to protest, he makes it clear that this is not merely ‘Poker-Faced Psychiatry’ but a well-thought-out policy. In due time his refusal may either enrage the patient or precipitate acute anxiety symptoms. The next step depends on the malignancy of the patient’s condition. If she is too upset, her acute reactions should be dealt with by appropriate psychiatric or analytic procedures to re-establish the therapeutic situation. The first goal, in the dissembled form, is to split off the Adult from the hypocritical Child so that the game can be analysed.

对立面。治疗师首先必须判断这种游戏是否出于善意，从而是否应该允许其继续进行，以利于患者的利益，直到其“成人”人格足够稳固，可以承担采取应对措施的风险。如果并非出于善意，则应在患者做好充分准备、能够理解所发生的一切之后，在第一个合适的时机采取应对措施。此时，治疗师应坚定地拒绝提供建议，当患者开始抗议时，他应明确表示这并非仅仅是“扑克脸精神病学”，而是一项深思熟虑的策略。随着时间的推移，他的拒绝可能会激怒患者，或引发急性焦虑症状。下一步取决于患者病情的严重程度。如果患者情绪过于激动，则应通过适当的精神科或分析程序来处理其急性反应，以重建治疗情境。从表面上看，首要目标是将“成人”人格与虚伪的“儿童”人格区分开来，以便对这种游戏进行分析。

In social situations, intimate entanglements with innocent GYWM players should be avoided, as any intelligent actor’s agent will impress upon his clients. On the other hand, women who play dissembled GYWM are sometimes interesting and intelligent if they can be de-GYWMed, and may turn out to be quite a delightful addition to the family social circle.

在社交场合，应避免与那些看似无辜的“年轻貌美男性”（GYWM）扮演者发展亲密关系，任何一位精明的经纪人都会告诫自己的客户这一点。另一方面，如果能够揭开她们伪装的“年轻貌美男性”身份，她们有时会展现出有趣而聪慧的一面，甚至可能成为家庭社交圈中令人愉悦的一员。

5 · PSYCHIATRY

5 · 精神病学

Thesis. Psychiatry as a procedure must be distinguished from ‘Psychiatry’ as a game. According to the available evidence, presented in proper clinical form in scientific publications, the following approaches, among others, are of value in treating psychiatric conditions: shock therapy, hypnosis, drugs, psychoanalysis, orthopsychiatry and group therapy. There are others which are less commonly used and will not be discussed here. Any of these can be used in the game of ‘Psychiatry’, which is based on the position ‘I am a healer’, supported by a diploma: ‘It says here I am a healer’. It will be noted that in any case this is a constructive, benevolent position, and that people who play ‘Psychiatry’ can do a great deal of good, providing they are professionally trained.

论文：精神病学作为一种医疗程序，必须与“精神病学”作为一种游戏区分开来。根据现有证据（以科学出版物中恰当的临床形式呈现），以下方法（以及其他方法）对治疗精神疾病有价值：电击疗法、催眠疗法、药物治疗、精神分析、正统精神病学和团体治疗。还有一些不太常用的方法，本文不作讨论。所有这些方法都可以用于“精神病学”这种游戏，该游戏基于“我是治疗师”的立场，并附有“这里写着我是治疗师”的证书。需要指出的是，无论如何，这都是一种建设性的、善意的立场，而且只要接受过专业训练，参与“精神病学”游戏的人就能做出很多贡献。

It is likely, however, that there will be some gain in therapeutic results if therapeutic ardour is moderated. The antithesis was best expressed long ago by Ambroise Paré, who said in effect: ‘I treat them, but God cures them.’ Every medical student learns about this dictum, along with others such as primum non nocere, and phrases such as vis medicatrix naturae. Nonmedical therapists, however, are not so likely to be exposed to these ancient cautions. The position ‘I am a healer because it says here that I am a healer’ is likely to be an impairment, and may be replaced to advantage with something like: ‘I will apply what therapeutic procedures I have learned in the hope that they will be of some benefit.’ This avoids the possibility of games based on: ‘Since I am a healer, if you don’t get better it’s your fault’ (e.g., ‘I’m Only Trying To Help You’), or ‘Since you’re a healer, I’ll get better for you’ (e.g., ‘Peasant’). All of this, of course, is known in principle to every conscientious therapist. Certainly every therapist who has ever presented a case at a reputable clinic has been made aware of it. Conversely, a good clinic may be defined as one which makes its therapists aware of these things.

然而，如果治疗热情有所节制，治疗效果或许会有所提升。安布鲁瓦兹·帕雷很久以前就曾精辟地表达过相反的观点，他曾说过：“我治疗他们，但上帝治愈他们。” 每位医学生都会学习这句格言，以及其他一些格言，例如“首先，不伤害”（primum non nocere）和“自然疗愈”（vis medicatrix naturae）。然而，非医学领域的治疗师却不太可能接触到这些古老的告诫。 “我之所以是治疗师，是因为这里说我是治疗师”这种想法很可能是一种缺陷，可以将其替换为类似这样的积极想法：“我会运用我所学的治疗方法，希望它们能有所帮助。”这样就能避免出现以下情况：比如“因为我是治疗师，如果你没好转，那就是你的错”（例如，“我只是想帮你”），或者“因为你是治疗师，所以我会为了你而好起来”（例如，“乡巴佬”）。当然，所有这些原则上都是每个尽职尽责的治疗师都明白的。事实上，每个在正规诊所接诊过的治疗师都肯定了解这些。反过来，一个好的诊所也可以定义为能够让其治疗师了解这些情况的诊所。

On the other side, the game of ‘Psychiatry’ is more apt to crop up with patients who have previously been treated by less competent therapists. A few patients, for example, carefully pick weak psychoanalysts, moving from one to another, demonstrating that they cannot be cured and meanwhile learning to play a sharper and sharper game of ‘Psychiatry’; eventually it becomes difficult for even a first-rate clinician to separate the wheat from the chaff. The duplex transaction on the patient’s side is:

另一方面，“精神病学”游戏更容易出现在那些之前接受过水平较低的治疗师治疗的患者身上。例如，有些患者会精心挑选水平较差的精神分析师，辗转于不同的治疗师之间，以此证明自己无法被治愈，同时不断学习如何玩转“精神病学”游戏，变得越来越狡猾；最终，即使是一流的临床医生也很难分辨真假。患者一方的双重交易是：

Adult: ‘I am coming to be cured.’

成年人：“我是来接受治疗的。”

Child: ‘You will never cure me, but you will teach me to be a better neurotic (play a better game of “Psychiatry”).’

孩子：“你永远也治不好我的病，但你可以教我如何成为一个更好的神经质患者（玩“精神病学”游戏玩得更好）。”

‘Mental Health’ is played similarly; here the Adult statement is, ‘Everything will get better if I apply the principles of mental health which I have read and heard about.’ One patient learned to play ‘Psychiatry’ from one therapist, ‘Mental Health’ from another, and then as a result of still another effort began to play a pretty good game of ‘Transactional Analysis’. When this was frankly discussed with her, she agreed to stop playing ‘Mental Health’, but requested that she be allowed to continue to play ‘Psychiatry’ because it made her feel comfortable. The transactional psychiatrist agreed. She continued therefore for several months to recite her dreams and her interpretations of them at weekly intervals. Finally, partly out of plain gratitude, perhaps, she decided that it might be interesting to find out what was really the matter with her. She became seriously interested in transactional analysis, with good results.

“心理健康”的玩法也类似；这里，成年人的陈述是：“如果我运用我读到和听到的心理健康原则，一切都会好起来。”一位病人先是从一位治疗师那里学会了“精神病学”，又从另一位治疗师那里学会了“心理健康”，然后经过一番努力，她开始相当熟练地运用“人际沟通分析”。当有人坦诚地和她讨论这个问题时，她同意停止“心理健康”的玩法，但请求允许她继续玩“精神病学”，因为这让她感到自在。那位人际沟通分析的精神科医生同意了。因此，在接下来的几个月里，她每周都会复述自己的梦境和梦境的解释。最终，或许是出于感激之情，她决定探究一下自己真正的问题所在。她开始对人际沟通分析产生了浓厚的兴趣，并取得了良好的效果。

A variant of ‘Psychiatry’ is ‘Archaeology’ (title by courtesy of Dr Norman Reider of San Francisco), in which the patient takes the position that if she can only find out who had the button, so to speak, everything will suddenly be all right. This results in a continual rumination over childhood happenings. Sometimes the therapist may be beguiled into a game of ‘Critique’, in which the patient describes her feelings in various situations and the therapist tells her what is wrong with them. ‘Self-Expression’, which is a common game in some therapy groups, is based on the dogma ‘Feelings are Good’. A patient who uses vulgar expletives, for example, may be applauded or at least implicitly lauded. A sophisticated group, however, will soon spot this as a game.

“精神病学”的一种变体是“考古学”（此名称由旧金山的诺曼·雷德医生提供），在这种疗法中，患者会认为，只要能找到所谓的“按钮”，一切就会迎刃而解。这导致患者不断反复思考童年往事。有时，治疗师可能会被诱入“批判”的游戏，患者描述自己在各种情境下的感受，而治疗师则指出这些感受的问题所在。“自我表达”是某些治疗小组中常见的游戏，其基础是“感受是好的”这一教条。例如，如果患者使用粗俗的脏话，可能会得到掌声，或者至少会得到间接的赞扬。然而，一个成熟的小组很快就会识破这种游戏。

Some members of therapy groups become quite adept at picking out games of ‘Psychiatry’, and will soon let a new patient know if they think he is playing ‘Psychiatry’ or ‘Transactional Analysis’ instead of using group procedures to obtain legitimate insight. A woman who transferred from a Self-Expression group in one city to a more sophisticated group in another city told a story about an incestuous relationship in her childhood. Instead of the awe which she had come to expect whenever she told this oft-repeated tale, she was greeted with indifference, whereupon she became enraged. She was astonished to discover that the new group was more interested in her transactional anger than in her historical incest, and in irate tones she hurled what apparently in her mind was the ultimate insult: she accused them of not being Freudian. Freud himself, of course, took psychoanalysis more seriously, and avoided making a game of it by saying that he himself was not a Freudian.

有些治疗小组的成员非常擅长识别“精神病学”游戏，他们很快就会告诉新来的病人，如果他们认为他是在玩“精神病学”或“人际沟通分析”，而不是通过小组程序来获得真正的领悟。一位女士从一个城市的自我表达小组转到另一个城市一个更成熟的小组，讲述了她童年时期一段乱伦关系的经历。每当她讲述这个反复出现的故事时，她都期待着小组成员们会感到敬畏，但这次他们却漠不关心，这让她勃然大怒。她惊讶地发现，新小组对她这种人际沟通式的愤怒比对她童年时期的乱伦经历更感兴趣，于是她怒气冲冲地抛出了在她看来是莫大的侮辱：她指责他们不是弗洛伊德主义者。当然，弗洛伊德本人对精神分析的态度更为严肃，他为了避免玩弄这种游戏，明确表示自己并非弗洛伊德主义者。

Recently unmasked is a new variant of ‘Psychiatry’ called ‘Tell Me This’, somewhat similar to the party pastime ‘Twenty Questions’. White relates a dream or an incident, and the other members, often including the therapist, then attempt to interpret it by asking pertinent questions. As long as White answers the questions, each member continues his inquiries until he finds a question White cannot answer. Then Black sits back with a knowing look which says: ‘Aha! If you could answer that one, you would certainly get better, so I have done my part.’ (This is a distant relative of ‘Why Don’t You – Yes But’.) Some therapy groups are based almost entirely on this game, and may go on for years with only minimal change or progress. ‘Tell Me This’ allows much latitude to White (the patient) who, for example, can play along with it by feeling ineffectual; or he can counter it by answering all the questions offered, in which case the anger and dismay of the other players soon becomes manifest, since he is throwing back at them, ‘I’ve answered all your questions and you haven’t cured me, so what does that make you?’

最近曝光了一种名为“告诉我”的新型“精神病学”游戏，它与派对游戏“二十个问题”有些类似。白方讲述一个梦境或一段经历，其他成员（通常包括治疗师）则试图通过提出相关问题来解读。只要白方能回答问题，每个成员就会继续提问，直到找到一个白方无法回答的问题。这时，黑方会带着一种心照不宣的表情靠在椅背上，仿佛在说：“啊哈！如果你能回答这个问题，你肯定会好起来的，所以我的功课已经完成了。”（这与“你为什么不——是的，但是……”游戏有几分相似。）有些治疗小组几乎完全基于这种游戏，可能持续数年却收效甚微。“告诉我”游戏给予白方（患者）很大的自由度，例如，他可以通过表现得无能为力来配合游戏；或者他可以通过回答所有提出的问题来反击，在这种情况下，其他玩家的愤怒和沮丧很快就会显现出来，因为他反驳他们说：“我已经回答了你们所有的问题，但你们并没有治好我，那你们又是什么呢？”

‘Tell Me This’ is also played in schoolrooms, where the pupils know that the ‘right’ answer to an open-ended question asked by a certain type of teacher is not to be found by processing the factual data, but by guessing or outguessing which of several possible answers will make the teacher happy. A pedantic variant occurs in teaching ancient Greek; the teacher always has the upper hand over the pupil, and can make him look stupid and prove it in print by pointing to some obscure feature of the text. This is also often played in teaching Hebrew.

在课堂上，学生们也经常玩“告诉我”的游戏。他们知道，对于某些类型的老师提出的开放式问题，“正确”答案并非通过分析事实数据来找到，而是通过猜测或猜中几个可能的答案中哪一个会让老师满意。在教授古希腊语时，也会出现一种略显迂腐的变体；老师总是占据上风，能够让学生出丑，并通过指出文本中某些晦涩难懂之处来证明这一点。这种游戏也经常出现在希伯来语教学中。

6 · STUPID

6 · 愚蠢

Thesis. In its milder form, the thesis of ‘Stupid’ is, ‘I laugh with you at my own clumsiness and stupidity.’ Seriously disturbed people, however, may play it in a sullen way which says, ‘I am stupid, that’s the way I am, so do me something.’ Both forms are played from a depressive position. ‘Stupid’ must be distinguished from ‘Schlemiel’, where the position is more aggressive, and the clumsiness is a bid for forgiveness. It must also be distinguished from ‘Clown’, which is not a game but a pastime which reinforces the position ‘I am cute and harmless.’ The critical transaction in ‘Stupid’ is for White to make Black call him stupid or respond as though he were stupid. Hence White acts like a Schlemiel but does not ask for forgiveness; in fact forgiveness makes him uneasy, because it threatens his position. Or he behaves clownishly, but with no implication that he is kidding; he wants his behaviour to be taken seriously, as evidence of real stupidity. There is considerable external gain, since the less White learns, the more effectively he can play. Hence at school he need not study, and at work he need not go out of his way to learn anything that might lead to advancement. He has known from an early age that everyone will be satisfied with him as long as he is stupid, despite any expressions to the contrary. People are surprised when in time of stress, if he decides to come through, it turns out that he is not stupid at all – any more than is the ‘stupid’ younger son in the fairy tale.

论点。“愚蠢”这一棋局的论点，在其较为温和的形式中，是“我和你一起嘲笑我的笨拙和愚蠢”。然而，严重受困扰的人可能会以一种阴郁的方式演绎它，仿佛在说：“我就是愚蠢，我就是这样，所以请你帮帮我吧。”这两种形式都源于一种沮丧的心态。“愚蠢”必须与“笨蛋”区分开来，后者的姿态更具攻击性，笨拙的行为是为了寻求原谅。它也必须与“小丑”区分开来，“小丑”并非游戏，而是一种消遣，它强化了“我可爱无害”的形象。“愚蠢”的关键在于白方要让黑方称他为愚蠢，或者做出如同他愚蠢的反应。因此，白方表现得像个笨蛋，但并不请求原谅；事实上，原谅会让他感到不安，因为它威胁到他的立场。或者，他表现得像个小丑，但并不暗示他是在开玩笑；他希望自己的行为被认真对待，以此证明他确实愚蠢。这样做有相当大的外部好处，因为白方学得越少，他下棋就越有效。因此，他在学校无需学习，在工作中也无需刻意学习任何可能带来晋升的知识。他从小就知道，只要他表现得愚蠢，无论别人怎么说，都会对他满意。人们惊讶地发现，在压力之下，如果他真的挺身而出，就会发现他其实一点也不蠢——就像童话故事里那个“笨”的小儿子一样。

Antithesis. The antithesis of the milder form is simple. By not playing, by not laughing at the clumsiness or railing at the stupidity, the anti-‘Stupid’ player will make a friend for life. One of the subtleties is that this game is often played by cyclothymic or manic-depressive personalities. When such people are euphoric, it seems as though they really want their associates to join in their laughter at themselves. It is often hard not to, for they give the impression that they will resent an abstainer – which in a way they do, since he threatens their position and spoils the game. But when they are depressed, and their resentment against those who laughed with or at them comes into the open, the abstainer knows that he has acted correctly. He may be the only one the patient is willing to have in the room or talk to when he is withdrawn, and all the former ‘friends’ who enjoyed the game are now treated as enemies.

反面。温和形式的反面很简单。通过不参与游戏，不嘲笑笨拙或斥责愚蠢，“反愚蠢”玩家将结交终生挚友。其中一个微妙之处在于，这种游戏常常由循环型或躁郁型人格障碍者玩。当这类人情绪高涨时，他们似乎真的希望同伴们加入到嘲笑自己的行列中。这往往很难做到，因为他们给人的印象是会怨恨不参与游戏的人——某种程度上，他们的确会怨恨，因为不参与游戏的人会威胁到他们的地位，破坏游戏。但当他们情绪低落，对那些曾经和他们一起嘲笑或嘲笑他们的人的怨恨显露出来时，不参与游戏的人就知道自己的做法是正确的。他可能是患者在封闭自我时唯一愿意待在房间里或与之交谈的人，而所有曾经享受游戏乐趣的“朋友”现在都被视为敌人。

It is no use telling White that he is not really stupid. He may actually be of quite limited intelligence and well aware of it, which is how the game got started in the first place. There may be special areas, however, in which he is superior: often psychological insight is one. It does no harm to show whatever respect is deserved for such aptitudes, but this is different from clumsy attempts at ‘reassurance’. The latter may give him the bitter satisfaction of realizing that other people are even more stupid than he, but this is small consolation. Such ‘reassurance’ is certainly not the most intelligent therapeutic procedure; usually it is a move in a game of ‘I’m Only Trying to Help You’. The antithesis of ‘Stupid’ is not to substitute another game, but simply to refrain from playing ‘Stupid’.

告诉怀特他其实并不笨是没用的。他可能智力有限，而且对此心知肚明，这正是游戏最初开始的原因。然而，他或许在某些领域技高一筹：心理洞察力往往就是其中之一。对他的这些才能表示应有的尊重并无坏处，但这与笨拙的“安慰”截然不同。后者或许会让他痛苦地意识到其他人比他更笨，但这毫无安慰可言。这种“安慰”绝非明智之举；它通常只是“我只是想帮你”游戏中的一招。“愚蠢”的反义词并非是换一种游戏，而是干脆避免玩“愚蠢”的游戏。

The antithesis of the sullen form is a more complicated problem, because the sullen player is trying to provoke not laughter or derision but helplessness or exasperation, which he is well equipped to handle in accordance with his challenge. ‘So do me something.’ Thus he wins either way. If Black does nothing, it is because he feels helpless, and if he does something, it is because he is exasperated. Hence these people are prone also to play ‘Why Don’t You – Yes But’, from which they can get the same satisfactions in milder form. There is no easy solution in this case, nor is there likely to be one forthcoming until the psychodynamics of this game are more clearly understood.

与阴郁型棋风相反的局面则更为复杂，因为阴郁型棋手试图激起的并非嘲笑或讥讽，而是无助或恼怒，而他完全有能力根据自己的挑战来应对这些情绪。“那就做点什么吧。”这样一来，无论哪种方式，他都能获胜。如果黑方什么也不做，那是因为他感到无助；如果他有所行动，那是因为他感到恼怒。因此，这些人也倾向于下“你为什么不——是的，但是……”这种棋风，他们可以从中获得同样、但更为温和的满足感。这种情况没有简单的解决办法，而且在更清楚地理解这种棋风的心理动力学之前，也不太可能出现解决办法。

7 · WOODEN LEG

7. 木腿

Thesis. The most dramatic form of ‘Wooden Leg’ is ‘The Plea of Insanity’. This may be translated into transactional terms as follows: ‘What do you expect of someone as emotionally disturbed as I am – that I would refrain from killing people?’ To which the jury is asked to reply: ‘Certainly not, we would hardly impose that restriction on you!’ The ‘Plea of Insanity’, played as a legal game, is acceptable to American culture and is different from the almost universally respected principle that an individual may be suffering from a psychosis so profound that no reasonable person would expect him to be responsible for his actions. In Japan drunkenness, and in Russia war-time military service, are accepted as excuses for evading responsibility for all kinds of outrageous behaviour (according to this writer’s information).

论点。“木腿”最戏剧化的形式是“精神错乱辩护”。这可以翻译成如下的对话：“你们指望像我这样精神失常的人能不杀人吗？”陪审团会被要求回答：“当然不会，我们绝不会对你施加这样的限制！”这种作为法律游戏的“精神错乱辩护”在美国文化中是可以接受的，它不同于几乎普遍被认可的原则，即一个人可能患有严重的精神病，以至于任何理智的人都不会期望他为自己的行为负责。在日本，醉酒；在俄罗斯，战时服兵役（据笔者所知）都被视为逃避各种过激行为责任的借口。

The thesis of ‘Wooden Leg’ is, ‘What do you expect of a man with a wooden leg?’ Put that way, of course, no one would expect anything of a man with a wooden leg except that he should steer his own wheel chair. On the other hand, during World War II there was a man with a wooden leg who used to give demonstrations of jitterbug dancing, and very competent jitterbug dancing, at Army Hospital amputation centres. There are blind men who practice law and hold political offices (one such is currently mayor of the writer’s home town), deaf men who practise psychiatry and handless men who can use a typewriter.

《木腿》一书的主旨是：“你对一个装了木腿的人有什么期待？” 这么说来，人们当然不会对一个装了木腿的人抱有任何期待，除了让他自己操控轮椅。然而，二战期间，确实有一位装了木腿的男子在陆军医院的截肢中心表演吉特巴舞，而且舞技精湛。此外，还有盲人从事法律工作，担任公职（其中一位目前是作者家乡的市长），聋人从事精神病学，以及双手残疾的人能够熟练地使用打字机。

As long as someone with a real, exaggerated or even imaginary disability is content with his lot, perhaps no one should interfere. But the moment he presents himself for psychiatric treatment, the question arises if he is using his life to his own best advantage, and if he can rise above his disability. In this country the therapist will be working in opposition to a large mass of educated public opinion. Even the close relatives of the patient who complained most loudly about the inconveniences caused by his infirmity, may eventually turn on the therapist if the patient makes definitive progress. This is readily understandable to a game analyst, but it makes his task no less difficult. All the people who were playing ‘I’m Only Trying to Help You’ are threatened by the impending disruption of the game if the patient shows signs of striking out on his own, and sometimes they use almost incredible measures to terminate the treatment.

只要一个身患残疾的人，无论残疾是真实的、夸大的还是想象出来的，对自己的处境感到满意，或许就不应该有人干涉。但一旦他寻求精神治疗，问题就出现了：他是否充分利用了自己的人生，他是否能够克服自身的残疾？在这个国家，治疗师将与大量受过良好教育的公众舆论对抗。即使是那些曾经对病人残疾带来的不便抱怨最多的亲属，如果病人取得了显著的进步，最终也可能转而反对治疗师。这对于一位博弈论分析师来说很容易理解，但这丝毫不会减轻他的工作难度。所有那些曾经扮演“我只是想帮你”角色的人，都会因为病人表现出独立行动的迹象而感到威胁，有时他们甚至会采取近乎疯狂的手段来终止治疗。

Both sides are illustrated by the case of the stuttering client of Miss Black’s, mentioned in the discussion of the game ‘Indigence’. This man played a classical form of ‘Wooden Leg’. He was unable to find employment, which he correctly attributed to the fact that he was a stutterer, since the only career that interested him, he said, was that of salesman. As a free citizen he had a right to seek employment in whatever field he chose, but as a stutterer, his choice raised some question as to the purity of his motives. The reaction of the helpful agency when Miss Black attempted to break up this game was very unfavourable to her.

布莱克小姐那位口吃的客户的例子，很好地说明了双方的观点。这个客户在讨论“贫困”游戏时被提及。他玩的是一种经典的“木腿”游戏。他找不到工作，他正确地将此归咎于自己口吃，因为他说他唯一感兴趣的职业就是推销员。作为一个自由公民，他有权选择任何领域的工作，但作为一个口吃者，他的选择让人质疑他动机的纯洁性。当布莱克小姐试图阻止他玩这个游戏时，那家热心机构的反应对她非常不利。

‘Wooden Leg’ is especially pernicious in clinical practice, because the patient may find a therapist who plays the same game with the same plea, so that progress is impossible. This is relatively easy to arrange in the case of the ‘Ideological Plea’, ‘What do you expect of a man who lives in a society like ours?’ One patient combined this with the ‘Psychosomatic Plea’, ‘What do you expect of a man with psychosomatic symptoms?’ He found a succession of therapists who would accept one plea but not the other, so that none of them either made him feel comfortable in his current position by accepting both pleas, or budged him from it by rejecting both. Thus he proved that psychiatry couldn’t help people.

“木腿”理论在临床实践中尤其有害，因为患者可能会找到一个同样玩弄手段、提出同样诉求的治疗师，导致治疗进展停滞不前。对于“意识形态诉求”（例如“你对生活在我们这样的社会里的人有什么期望？”）来说，这种情况相对容易发生。一位患者将这种诉求与“心身疾病诉求”（例如“你对一个有心身症状的人有什么期望？”）结合起来。他遇到的治疗师一个接一个地接受其中一种诉求，却不接受另一种，因此，没有一位治疗师会同时接受这两种诉求，让他感到安心；也没有一位治疗师会同时拒绝这两种诉求，让他摆脱困境。就这样，他证明了精神病学对人们毫无帮助。

Some of the pleas which patients use to excuse symptomatic behaviour are colds, head injuries, situational stress, the stress of modern living, American culture and the economic system. A literate player has no difficulty in finding authorities to support him. ‘I drink because I’m Irish.’ ‘This wouldn’t happen if I lived in Russia or Tahiti.’ The fact is that patients in mental hospitals in Russia and Tahiti are very similar to those in American state hospitals. 1 Special pleas of ‘If It Weren’t For Them’ or ‘They Let Me Down’ should always be evaluated very carefully in clinical practice – and also in social research projects.

患者用来为自己异常行为开脱的一些理由包括感冒、头部受伤、情境压力、现代生活的压力、美国文化以及经济体制。一个有文化的人很容易找到权威人士来支持他。“我喝酒是因为我是爱尔兰人。”“如果我住在俄罗斯或塔希提岛，就不会发生这种事。” 事实上，俄罗斯和塔希提岛精神病院的患者与美国州立医院的患者非常相似。 1 在临床实践中——以及在社会研究项目中——对于“如果不是他们”或“他们让我失望了”之类的特殊辩解，都应该始终进行非常谨慎的评估。

Slightly more sophisticated are such pleas as: What do you expect of a man who ( a ) comes from a broken home; ( b ) is neurotic; ( c ) is in analysis or ( d ) is suffering from a disease known as alcoholism? These are topped by, ‘If I stop doing this I won’t be able to analyse it, and then I’ll never get better.’

稍微复杂一些的请求是这样的：你对一个（a）来自破碎家庭；（b）神经质；（c）正在接受心理分析；或（d）患有酗酒这种疾病的人有什么期望？更甚者，还有“如果我停止做这件事，我就无法进行心理分析，那样我就永远不会好起来了。”

The obverse of ‘Wooden Leg’ is ‘Rickshaw’, with the thesis, ‘If they only had (rickshaws) (duckbill platypuses) (girls who spoke ancient Egyptian) around this town, I never would have got into this mess.’

《木腿》的正面是《人力车》，其主题是：“如果这个镇子里有（人力车）（鸭嘴兽）（会说古埃及语的女孩），我就不会陷入这种困境了。”

Antithesis. Anti-‘Wooden Leg’ is not difficult if the therapist can distinguish clearly between his own Parent and Adult, and if the therapeutic aim is explicitly understood by both parties.

对立。如果治疗师能够清楚地区分自己的父母角色和成人角色，并且双方都明确理解治疗目标，那么对抗“木腿”并不难。

On the Parental side, he can be either a ‘good’ Parent or a ‘harsh’ one. As a ‘good’ Parent he can accept the patient’s plea, especially if it fits in with his own viewpoints, perhaps with the rationalization that people are not responsible for their actions until they have completed their therapy. As a ‘harsh’ Parent he can reject the plea and engage in a contest of wills with the patient. Both of these attitudes are already familiar to the ‘Wooden Leg’ player, and he knows how to extract the maximum satisfactions from each of them.

在扮演父母角色时，他可以是“好”父母，也可以是“严厉”父母。作为“好”父母，他可以接受病人的请求，尤其当病人的请求与他自己的观点相符时，比如他认为人们在完成治疗之前无需为自己的行为负责。作为“严厉”父母，他可以拒绝病人的请求，并与病人展开意志的较量。这两种态度对于“木腿”玩家来说都驾轻就熟，他知道如何从中获取最大的满足感。

As an Adult, the therapist declines both of these opportunities. When the patient asks, ‘What do you expect of a neurotic?’ (or whatever plea he is using at the moment) the reply is, ‘I don’t expect anything. The question is, what do you expect of yourself ?’ The only demand he makes is that the patient give a serious answer to this question, and the only concession he makes is to allow the patient a reasonable length of time to answer it: anywhere from six weeks to six months, depending on the relationship between them and the patient’s previous preparation.

作为成年治疗师，他拒绝了这两种机会。当病人问：“你对一个神经质的人有什么期望？”（或者他当时用的任何借口）时，他的回答是：“我什么都不期望。问题是，你对自己有什么期望？”他唯一的要求是病人认真回答这个问题，而他唯一的让步是给予病人一段合理的时间来回答：从六周到六个月不等，具体取决于他们之间的关系以及病人之前的准备情况。

REFERENCE

参考

1. Berne, E., ‘The Cultural Problem: Psychopathology in Tahiti’, American Journal of Psychiatry, 116: 1076–1081, 1960.

1. Berne, E., ‘文化问题：塔希提岛的精神病理学’，《美国精神病学杂志》，116：1076–1081，1960 年。

#↩

12 · Good Games

12 · 好游戏

T HE psychiatrist, who is in the best and perhaps the only position to study games adequately, unfortunately deals almost entirely with people whose games have led them into difficulties. This means that the games which are offered for clinical investigation are all in some sense ‘bad’ ones. And since by definition games are based on ulterior transactions, they must all have some element of exploitation. For these two reasons, practical on the one hand and theoretical on the other, the search for ‘good’ games becomes a difficult quest. A ‘good’ game might be described as one whose social contribution outweighs the complexity of its motivations, particularly if the player has come to terms with those motivations without futility or cynicism. That is, a ‘good’ game would be one which contributes both to the well-being of the other players and to the unfolding of the one who is ‘it’. Since even under the best forms of social action and organization a large proportion of time has to be spent in playing games, the search for ‘good’ ones must be assiduously pursued. Several examples are offered here, but they are admittedly deficient in both number and quality. They include ‘Busman’s Holiday’, ‘Cavalier’, ‘Happy to Help’, ‘Homely Sage’ and ‘They’ll Be Glad They Knew Me’.

精神科医生或许是唯一能够充分研究游戏的专家，但遗憾的是，他们几乎只接触那些因游戏而陷入困境的人。这意味着，所有用于临床研究的游戏在某种意义上都是“不良”游戏。而且，由于游戏本质上都基于不可告人的目的，它们必然都包含某种剥削的成分。基于这两个原因——一方面是实践层面的，另一方面是理论层面的——寻找“好”游戏变得异常艰难。“好”游戏可以被描述为：其社会贡献超过了其动机的复杂性，尤其当玩家能够坦然接受这些动机，而不感到徒劳或愤世嫉俗时。也就是说，“好”游戏既能促进其他玩家的福祉，又能促进“游戏者”自身的成长。即便在最佳的社会行动和组织形式下，人们也需要花费大量时间玩游戏，因此，寻找“好”游戏必须孜孜不倦地进行。这里列举了一些例子，但不得不承认，它们在数量和质量上都存在不足。这些例子包括《Busman’s Holiday》、《Cavalier》、《Happy to Help》、《Homely Sage》和《They’ll Be Glad They Knew Me》。

1 · BUSMAN’S HOLIDAY

1.《巴士司机的假期》

Thesis. Strictly speaking, this is a pastime rather than a game, and evidently a constructive one for all concerned. An American mail carrier who goes to Tokyo to help a Japanese postman on his rounds, or an American ear-nose-and-throat specialist who spends his holiday working in a Haitian hospital, will very likely feel just as refreshed and have just as good stories to tell as if he had gone lion hunting in Africa or spent the time driving through transcontinental highway traffic. The Peace Corps has now given official sanction to Busman’s Holiday.

论点：严格来说，这与其说是游戏，不如说是一种消遣，而且显然对所有参与者来说都是一种有益的消遣。一位美国邮递员去东京帮助一位日本邮递员送邮件，或者一位美国耳鼻喉科专家利用假期在海地医院工作，他们很可能会感到精神焕发，并拥有同样精彩的故事可以讲述，就像他们去非洲猎狮或驾车穿越洲际公路一样。和平队现在已经正式认可了“工作假期”这种说法。

‘Busman’s Holiday’ becomes a game, however, if the work is secondary to some ulterior motive and is undertaken merely as a show in order to accomplish something else. Even under those circumstances, however, it still keeps its constructive quality and is one of the more commendable covers for other activities (which may also be constructive).

然而，如果工作并非出于其他目的，而仅仅是为了完成某项任务而进行的作秀，那么“工作假期”就变成了一场游戏。即便如此，它仍然保持着其建设性，并且是其他活动（也可能具有建设性）的较为值得称道的掩护方式之一。

2 · CAVALIER

2 · 骑士

Thesis. This is a game played by men who are not under sexual pressure – occasionally by younger men who have a satisfactory marriage or liaison, more often by older men who are gracefully resigned to monogamy or celibacy. Upon encountering a suitable female subject, White takes every opportunity to remark upon her good qualities, never transgressing the limits appropriate to her station in life, the immediate social situation and the requirements of good taste. But within those limits he allows full play to his creativity, enthusiasm and originality. The object is not to seduce but to exhibit his virtuosity in the art of effective compliment. The internal social advantage lies in the pleasure given to the woman by this innocent artistry, and by her responsive appreciation of White’s skill. In suitable cases, where both are aware of the nature of the game, it may be stretched with increasing delight on both sides, to the point of extravagance. A man of the world, of course, will know when to stop, and will not continue beyond the point at which he ceases to amuse (out of consideration for her) or where the quality of his offerings begins to deteriorate (out of consideration for his own pride of craftsmanship). ‘Cavalier’ is played for its external social advantages in the case of poets, who are as much, or more, interested in the appreciation of qualified critics and the public at large as they are in the response of the lady who inspired them.

论点：这是一种由不受性压力影响的男性参与的游戏——有时是婚姻或婚外情美满的年轻男性，更多时候是欣然接受一夫一妻制或独身生活的年长男性。当遇到合适的女性对象时，怀特会抓住一切机会赞美她的优点，但绝不会越过与其社会地位、所处社交场合以及良好品味相符的界限。然而，在这些界限之内，他会充分发挥自己的创造力、热情和独创性。其目的并非诱惑，而是展现自己高超的赞美技巧。这种游戏的内在社交优势在于，女性会因这种纯真的艺术而感到愉悦，并对此表示赞赏。在双方都了解游戏本质的情况下，这种游戏可能会在双方的愉悦中不断延伸，直至达到一种奢靡的程度。当然，一个世故的人懂得适可而止，不会因为不再逗乐她（出于对她的体谅）或因为作品质量开始下降（出于对自己技艺的自尊）而继续下去。对于诗人而言，《骑士》这部作品更注重其外部的社会价值，因为他们同样，甚至更在意专业评论家和广大公众的赞赏，而非那位启发他们的女士的反应。

The Europeans in romance, and the British in poetry, seem always to have been more adept at this game than the Americans. In our country it has fallen largely into the hands of the Fruit Stand school of poetry: your eyes are like avocados, your lips like cucumbers, etc. ‘Cavalier’, Fruit Stand Type, can hardly compare in elegance with the productions of Herrick and Lovelace, or even with the cynical but imaginative works of Rochester, Roscommon and Dorset.

在浪漫爱情方面，欧洲人似乎总是比美国人更擅长此道，在诗歌方面，英国人也同样如此。在我们国家，这种诗歌风格大多落入了“水果摊派”的窠臼：你的眼睛像牛油果，你的嘴唇像黄瓜，等等。“骑士”——这种“水果摊派”式的诗歌——其优雅程度几乎无法与赫里克和洛夫莱斯的作品相提并论，甚至也无法与罗切斯特、罗斯康芒和多塞特那些愤世嫉俗却又充满想象力的作品相提并论。

Antithesis. It takes some sophistication for the woman to play her part well, and a great deal of sulkiness or stupidity for her to refuse to play it at all. The proper complement is a variant of ‘Gee You’re Wonderful Mr Murgatroyd’ (GYWM): namely, ‘I Admire Your Productions, Mr M’. If the woman is mechanical or unperceptive, she may respond with plain GYWM, but that misses the point: what White is offering for appreciation is not himself, but his poetry. The brutal antithesis from a sulky woman is to play Second-Degree ‘Rapo’ (‘Buzz Off, Buster’). Third-Degree ‘Rapo’, which could conceivably occur, would of course be an unspeakably vile response under the circumstances. If the woman is merely stupid, she will play First-Degree ‘Rapo’, taking the compliments to feed her vanity and neglecting to appreciate White’s creative efforts and abilities. In general, the game is spoiled if the woman treats it as an attempt at seduction rather than as a literary exhibition.

反义词。女人要演绎好这个角色需要一定的老练，而完全拒绝扮演则需要极大的怨恨或愚蠢。恰当的赞美是“哇，你真棒，默格特罗伊德先生”（GYWM）的变体，即“我欣赏你的作品，默格特罗伊德先生”。如果女人机械或缺乏洞察力，她可能会简单地回应“哇，你真棒”，但这完全不得要领：怀特先生想要表达赞赏的并非他本人，而是他的诗歌。一个怨恨的女人最残酷的反义词是二级“拉波”（“滚开，混蛋”）。三级“拉波”——虽然理论上存在——当然在这种情况下是极其恶劣的回应。如果女人只是愚蠢，她会一级“拉波”，把赞美当作满足虚荣心的工具，而忽略了对怀特先生的创作努力和才华的欣赏。一般来说，如果女性将写作视为勾引他人而非文学展示，那么写作就会失去意义。

Relatives. ‘Cavalier’ being a game, it must be distinguished from the operations and procedures carried on during a straight-forward courtship, which are simple transactions without ulterior motive. The female counterpart of ‘Cavalier’ may be conveniently called ‘Blarney’, since it is often played by gallant Irish ladies in their sunset years.
